<div id="review_382102364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382102364" />
    <a title="Kristy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2705039-kristy"><img alt="Kristy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453228324p2/2705039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382102364?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy" href="/user/show/2705039-kristy">Kristy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2705039-kristy?shelf=i-think-you-should-read-this">i-think-you-should-read-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2705039-kristy?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382102364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12400377255129420923">It's the end of the world as we know it, it's the end of the world as we know it, it's the end of the world as we know it........... and I feel fine.<br/><br/>Well, I have to admit I liked this one much better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2169506.The_Dead_and_the_Gone__Last_Survivors___2_' title='The Dead and the Gone (Last Survivors, #2) by Susan Beth Pfeffer' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dead and the Gone</a>. I know I am in the minority with this, but I feel like this one got some of the magic back. I picked this book up and you couldn't have gotten it out my hands today.... even to go to the beach (ask my hubs). Seriously, this one hooked me in. I am also in the minority with</span>
  <span id="freeText12400377255129420923" style="display:none">It's the end of the world as we know it, it's the end of the world as we know it, it's the end of the world as we know it........... and I feel fine.<br /><br />Well, I have to admit I liked this one much better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2169506.The_Dead_and_the_Gone__Last_Survivors___2_" title="The Dead and the Gone (Last Survivors, #2) by Susan Beth Pfeffer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead and the Gone</a>. I know I am in the minority with this, but I feel like this one got some of the magic back. I picked this book up and you couldn't have gotten it out my hands today.... even to go to the beach (ask my hubs). Seriously, this one hooked me in. I am also in the minority with feeling very sad this series is over.<br /><br />About that: Spoilers ahead amigos:<br /><br />What kind of crack-pot ending was that?!?!?!!? I feel like my book must have had pages torn out or something!!!! After 3 books of this surviving, I really hoped for some closure.... I am glad, however, she didn't end it all sunshine and rainbows. Alex is a character that is very hard for me to understand. Why does he feel the need to follow the rules, especially from Carlos in regards to his sister?!?!?!? Poor Julie. Why did Mrs. Pfeffer feel the need to marry Matt off to Syl???? Why was there so much importance on that freaking baby?!?!?!? (I know, the future, holy cannoli, enough already.) Why do they not just move already?!?!?!? (especially when the house starts flooding????) I get it would be hard to just leave your comfort zone, but geez. At some points, I am very suprised the Evans family have survived for this long.....<br /><br />See, these books would be so good for school!!! I said it in my first book review and I stand by it. There is many topics to discuss, there would be so many different opinions and ways of surviving. <br /><br /><br />Gosh. I need to start stock-piling. Maybe these extreme couponers are smarter than we give them credit for........<br /><br /><br />4 stars. I highly recommend you read these books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12400377255129420923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_103670465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103670465" />
    <a title="Brian Rheinhardt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2788576-brian-rheinhardt"><img alt="Brian Rheinhardt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1259025742p2/2788576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103670465?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Rheinhardt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Rheinhardt" href="/user/show/2788576-brian-rheinhardt">Brian Rheinhardt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103670465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4415685807237505642">I'm almost finished this one, the third book in Pfeffer's "oh crap the moon was hit be a meteor and moved closer to the Earth causing complete havoc" series. This diary-style YA book has the female protagonist from book 1 (Miranda) meeting the male protagonist in book 2 (Alex). The female is back to telling the story.<br/><br/>My criticisms of book 1 arise again in this book. Most of this story could be summarized with "We're hungry and bored. Will we have enough food to survive?" Although realistic consi</span>
  <span id="freeText4415685807237505642" style="display:none">I'm almost finished this one, the third book in Pfeffer's "oh crap the moon was hit be a meteor and moved closer to the Earth causing complete havoc" series. This diary-style YA book has the female protagonist from book 1 (Miranda) meeting the male protagonist in book 2 (Alex). The female is back to telling the story.<br /><br />My criticisms of book 1 arise again in this book. Most of this story could be summarized with "We're hungry and bored. Will we have enough food to survive?" Although realistic considering the premise, that doesn't necessarily make for a great story. There are a few surprises sprinkled throughout the plot, but this apocolyptic survival story is more Little House on the Prairie than it is The Road Warrior.<br /><br />I don't regret reading This World We Live In, but I wouldn't necessarily recommend it. Being the last (hopefully) in the series, I felt obligated to read it, especially since book 2 was much better than 1. This book is kinda like that last piece of pizza. You're really too full to eat it, but you don't want it to just sit there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4415685807237505642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/868733229" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/868733229?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=concierge">concierge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=nature">nature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868733229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9876291491746139988">Book three is the Last Survivors series takes us back to Howell, Pennsylvania. It’s been a year since an asteroid knocked the moon out of its orbit and closer to the earth. Miranda Evans, her mother and two brothers have managed to survive, but most of the townspeople have left and food is increasingly scarce. A tentative Spring brings new hope, at least until Miranda’s father and stepmother arrive with a new baby, and three strangers in tow. <br/><br/>This was really a major disappointment. Miranda has b</span>
  <span id="freeText9876291491746139988" style="display:none">Book three is the Last Survivors series takes us back to Howell, Pennsylvania. It’s been a year since an asteroid knocked the moon out of its orbit and closer to the earth. Miranda Evans, her mother and two brothers have managed to survive, but most of the townspeople have left and food is increasingly scarce. A tentative Spring brings new hope, at least until Miranda’s father and stepmother arrive with a new baby, and three strangers in tow. <br /><br />This was really a major disappointment. Miranda has become less mature than when we left her at the end of book 1. She whines and complains, throws tantrums, and runs off in a huff. Then there is her over-the-top watched-too-many-soap-operas-and-read-too-many-bodice-rippers “But I love you!” dialogue with Alex. Puh-leeze! Alex has also retreated into a silent, obstinate teen with none of the leadership and resourcefulness he displayed in book 2. <br /><br />Well, at least it reminds me why I generally dislike post-apocalyptic / dystopian fiction. It was a fast read, but seriously, don’t waste your time.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9876291491746139988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5686432284686560087" style="display:none">The third in the series is treading on thin ice (get it- the Earth is now freezing) as the combination of Miranda and Alex's families occur. <span id="freeTextContainer15042119957990885948">I really enjoyed book 3 of the Last Survivors series. I feel that it was a bit darker this time around, but I like how the dynamics had been set up for the most part. I wish we got to hear more from Miranda's perspective of their voyage after leaving their home, but it was a great way to tie off her story! I'm really excited to read the last book in the series!</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_124393920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124393920" />
    <a title="Shaun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3790946-shaun"><img alt="Shaun" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124393920?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaun" href="/user/show/3790946-shaun">Shaun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer124393920&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124393920" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10180038937137673416">I literally just finished this a couple of minutes ago, and... it was okay, I guess. The series as a whole was just "okay", even though I enjoyed the first book a lot. The problem is that they don't really come to a resolution, or an ending at all, really. I don't have a problem with open-ended stories, but in a series, I expect something resembling an ending. *shrug*<br/><br/>The biggest problem I had with this book was Matt, though. I don't know if Susan Beth Pfeffer just forgot what he was like, but wh</span>
  <span id="freeText10180038937137673416" style="display:none">I literally just finished this a couple of minutes ago, and... it was okay, I guess. The series as a whole was just "okay", even though I enjoyed the first book a lot. The problem is that they don't really come to a resolution, or an ending at all, really. I don't have a problem with open-ended stories, but in a series, I expect something resembling an ending. *shrug*<br /><br />The biggest problem I had with this book was Matt, though. I don't know if Susan Beth Pfeffer just forgot what he was like, but what the hell. He turned into a straight-on jackass. He wasn't perfect in the first one, but he didn't seem like the same character at all. Marrying Syl was... weird. It seemed so OOC, and the way he talked about her and how he was so possessive and obsessed over a girl he'd known for like a week was just borderline creepy. Ugh. He was definitely the worst character in the book; I hated reading anything that concerned him. (Syl, however, I did like, despite the fact she killed the cat.)<br /><br />This book just wasn't all that exciting. The first one wasn't, either, but maybe I just didn't notice it then or maybe I just got bored of it, but it really was just Miranda whining <i>constantly</i>. Her relationship with Alex was badly done; they hated each other and then were completely in 'wuv' after the next few pages. Miranda seemed to get more and more unlikable as the book went on (not as much as Matt, though, thankfully).<br /><br />Parts I enjoyed: the rest of the characters, actually, except maybe Alex, but he was always an ass so I guess maybe we weren't supposed to like him. Mom (Laura), Jon, Julie, Charlie (from the little we saw of him), Dad (Hal) and Lisa, and even baby Gabriel, I did enjoy reading about, and that might be why I feel kind of cheated for not knowing what happens to most of them. They're the reason I'm giving this book 3*s instead of 2*s.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10180038937137673416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_54990906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54990906" />
    <a title="Luann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/651844-luann"><img alt="Luann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348555393p2/651844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54990906?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luann" href="/user/show/651844-luann">Luann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/651844-luann?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/651844-luann?shelf=epistolary">epistolary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/651844-luann?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/651844-luann?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/651844-luann?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54990906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4757025098135656294">I'm glad I read this, but it didn't leave me feeling very happy. It's all so very bleak! I kept thinking, "The sun is NEVER going to come back?" If that's the case, we need a fourth book telling the story of a group of survivors leaving Earth on a rocketship seeking a brand new planet!<br/><br/>I did like that Susan Beth Pfeffer returned to the diary format for this book, although I kept thinking, "No one records this much actual conversation in their diary!" I also liked the sneaky way she caught us up o</span>
  <span id="freeText4757025098135656294" style="display:none">I'm glad I read this, but it didn't leave me feeling very happy. It's all so very bleak! I kept thinking, "The sun is NEVER going to come back?" If that's the case, we need a fourth book telling the story of a group of survivors leaving Earth on a rocketship seeking a brand new planet!<br /><br />I did like that Susan Beth Pfeffer returned to the diary format for this book, although I kept thinking, "No one records this much actual conversation in their diary!" I also liked the sneaky way she caught us up on the story from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213753.Life_As_We_Knew_It__Last_Survivors___1_" title="Life As We Knew It (Last Survivors, #1) by Susan Beth Pfeffer" rel="nofollow noopener">Life As We Knew It</a> by having Miranda write about a dream she had explaining the moon's absence to Baby Rachel. I also thought it was very natural how Alex and Julie (from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2169506.The_Dead_and_the_Gone__Last_Survivors___2_" title="The Dead and the Gone (Last Survivors, #2) by Susan Beth Pfeffer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead and the Gone</a>) showed up in the story.<br /><br />So, while this certainly isn't a very happy book, I recommend it to those who have read the other two. Once I started, I didn't want to stop. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213753.Life_As_We_Knew_It__Last_Survivors___1_" title="Life As We Knew It (Last Survivors, #1) by Susan Beth Pfeffer" rel="nofollow noopener">Life As We Knew It</a> is by far my favorite, but I'm glad to have read this one as well. 3.5 stars.<br /><br />I liked this quote, which was some advice Miranda's dad gave: "Life's sloppy. You think you know how tomorrow is going to be, you've made your plans, everything is set in place, and then the unimaginable happens. Life catches you by surprise. It always does. But there's good mixed in with the bad. It's there. You just have to recognize it."</span>
  <a data-text-id="4757025098135656294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XQ/C+TpxOEfNOMNxL/XLwy6D7lutScaarlUb0WDLlbxMt0b3c8Ryko2siljYoisW9nqv1tGAbBz1ygFZOH0PhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cr2LPTShRNOVw9dCKEmHN6B/eNUgvatD50xzy+tWlCdjBQ8zfRQOBtVXnmvfHmfieIY5WFx0AcW802lDs+AOHw==')})
  }
//]]>

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1318.Susan_Beth_Pfeffer"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1228492581p3/1318.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1546720696188683457">Susan Beth Pfeffer was born in New York City in 1948. She grew up in the city and its nearby suburbs and spent summers in the Catskill Mountains. When she was six her father wrote and published a book on constitutional law, and Pfeffer decided that she, too, wanted to be a writer. That year she wrote her first story, about the love between an Oreo cookie and a pair of scissors. However, it wasn't </span>
  <span id="freeText1546720696188683457" style="display:none">Susan Beth Pfeffer was born in New York City in 1948. She grew up in the city and its nearby suburbs and spent summers in the Catskill Mountains. When she was six her father wrote and published a book on constitutional law, and Pfeffer decided that she, too, wanted to be a writer. That year she wrote her first story, about the love between an Oreo cookie and a pair of scissors. However, it wasn't until 1970 that her first book, Just Morgan, was published. She wrote it during her last semester at New York University; since then, she has been a full-time writer for young people. <br /><br />She has won numerous awards and citations for her work, which range from picture books to middle-grade and young-adult novels, and include both contemporary and historical fiction. She is also the author of the popular Portraits of Little Women series for grades 3-6, and has written a book for adults on writing for children.<br /><br />To date, she has written more than 60 books. About David was awarded the South Carolina Young Adult Book Award. The Year Without Michael is an ALA Best Book for Young Adults and winner of the South Carolina Young Adult Book Award; it was also named by the American Library Association as one of the hundred best books for teenagers written between 1968-1993. <br /><br />When she is not working, she enjoys watching movies, both new and old, and collecting movie memorabilia, reading biographies and histories, and eating foods that are bad for her. She lives in Middletown, New York, with her two cats, Alexander and Emily.<br /><br />Named the American Library Associations Young Adult Library Services Association Best Book for Young Adults 2007 and Teens’ Top Ten Booklist in 2007. Finalist for the Andre Norton Award, Quill Awards, Hal Clement Awards</span>
  <a data-text-id="1546720696188683457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
